## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material. Temperature typically affects elastic modulus and flow stress through thermal softening, while strain governs the mechanical response through linear or nonlinear constitutive laws.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with linearly decreasing modulus)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus with exponential thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain without temperature)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (strain hardening with exponential thermal softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (linear + nonlinear strain terms)
- Johnson-Cook type (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal term: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T**c3) (power-law hardening with homologous temperature softening)
- Polynomial stress-strain with T: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon * T + c2 * epsilon**2 (mixed polynomial)
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 / T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Voce hardening with T: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Ludwik equation with T: sigma = c0 * T**c1 + c2 * epsilon**c3 (temperature-dependent yield plus power hardening)
- Hyperbolic sine (Garofalo): sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon) (used in creep/high-T deformation)
- Rational thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * c2 / (T + c3) (softening as inverse temperature dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear stress-strain with temperature-modulated slope → product form E(T)*epsilon where E(T) is a decreasing function of T
- Thermal softening at high temperatures → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T^n) or exp(-c*T) multiplying the mechanical response
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating Voce-type saturation behavior
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon^n with 0 < n < 1 indicating work hardening with diminishing rate
- Separable stress function → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) suggesting independent strain hardening and thermal softening mechanisms
- Thermally activated processes → exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) terms reflecting Arrhenius-type activation energy barriers
- Yield stress offset → additive constant c0 representing initial yield strength before hardening begins
- Competing hardening and softening → sum of increasing function of epsilon and decreasing function of T
- Phase transition or abrupt softening → tanh or sigmoid in T indicating rapid property change at critical temperature

## Analysis

The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
$$f(\epsilon, T) = -0.6057(T - 298.0) + \epsilon \cdot 3.1474 \cdot \exp(-(T - 298.0)^2)$$

This has two key structural components:
1. A **linear term in T** (independent of ε): $-c_0 T + c_0 c_1$
2. An **ε term multiplied by a Gaussian in T**: $\epsilon \cdot c_2 \cdot \exp(-(T-c_3)^2)$

The critical feature is the **Gaussian function of T** multiplying ε: $\exp(-(T - 298)^2)$. This is a non-trivial nonlinear function of T.

Let me check each candidate for the ability to produce this Gaussian-in-T structure:

**Candidates with exp() terms involving T:**
- Candidates 25, 29, 38, 40, 42, 43, 46: These contain terms like $\exp(T \cdot c)$, which is exponential in T, not Gaussian. A single $\exp(cT)$ cannot produce $\exp(-(T-c)^2)$.

**Candidates with sin() terms involving T:**
- Candidates 7, 8, 10, 11, 12, 14: These have $\sin(T \cdot c + ...)$, which cannot produce a Gaussian.

**Candidates with power-law terms $(T + c)^c$:**
- Candidates 13, 15, 16, 17, 19, 20, 22, 31, 35, 39, 45, 48: These have power-law dependencies on T, not Gaussian.

**Candidates with log(T) terms:**
- Candidates 23, 27: $\log(Tc + 1)$ cannot produce a Gaussian.

**Candidates with rational functions in ε (no T nonlinearity for the ε coefficient):**
- Candidates 33, 34, 37, 44, 47, 49: These are rational/polynomial in both T and ε, cannot produce a Gaussian.

**Candidates with only polynomial/rational/log/sin of ε:**
- Candidates 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 24, 26, 36, 41: These lack the Gaussian-in-T structure entirely.

**Candidates with $1/(T+c)^5$ terms:**
- Candidates 10, 17: Power-law decay, not Gaussian.

**Candidates with $\exp(c/T)$ or similar:**
- Candidate 32: Has $\exp(c_6/(T+c_7))$, which is not Gaussian in T.

**Candidate 28:** $Tc_0 + c_1\exp(c_2\epsilon) + c_3/(T+c_4)^5 + c_5$ — no Gaussian in T.

**Candidate 30, 50:** Rational functions of T and ε — no Gaussian.

None of the candidates contain a term of the form $\exp(-(T - c)^2)$ or any combination that could algebraically produce a Gaussian function of T. The Gaussian in T is the essential structural element of the GT, and no candidate can replicate it through any parameter choices.

Conclusion: No match

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.6057*(T - 298.0) + epsilon*3.1474*exp(-(T - 298.0)^2)`

This simplifies to: `-0.6057*T + 180.53 + epsilon*3.1474*exp(-(T-298)^2)`

Key structural features of GT:
- Linear in T (no epsilon dependence in the linear T term)
- A constant term
- epsilon multiplied by a Gaussian function of T: `epsilon * exp(-(T-298)^2)`

The Gaussian `exp(-(T-298)^2)` is a very specific function of T. Let me check which candidates could possibly reproduce this structure.

For a candidate to match, it needs:
1. A term linear in T (coefficient independent of epsilon)
2. A constant term
3. A term proportional to `epsilon * exp(quadratic in T)` — specifically a Gaussian in T

Let me scan through candidates looking for `exp()` terms that could produce `epsilon * exp(-(T-c)^2)`:

Most candidates have structures like `exp(c*epsilon)`, `sin(...)`, `log(...)`, rational functions in epsilon, or power functions — none of which can produce `exp(-(T-298)^2)`.

Let me check candidates with `exp(T*c)` terms:
- **Candidates 25, 29, 38, 40, 42, 43, 46**: These have `exp(T*c5)` or similar — this is `exp(linear in T)`, not `exp(quadratic in T)`. These cannot match a Gaussian.

Candidates with no T-dependent exponential at all clearly cannot match since `epsilon*exp(-(T-298)^2)` requires a Gaussian in T.

**Candidate 36**: Has no T at all — cannot match.

**Candidates with `(T+c)^c` power terms** (13, 15, 16, 17, 19, 20, 22, 31, 35, 39, 45, 48): Power functions cannot reproduce Gaussians.

**Candidates with `sin(T*c + ...)` terms** (7, 8, 10, 11, 12, 14, 21, 22, 31, 43): `sin` cannot reproduce a Gaussian.

**Candidates with `log(T*c + 1)` terms** (23, 27): Logarithms cannot reproduce Gaussians.

**Candidate 28, 10, 17**: Have `1/(T+c)^5` — not Gaussian.

**Candidate 32**: Has `exp(c6/(T+c7))` — this is not a Gaussian in T.

**Candidate 50, 30, 18**: Have `1/(T*c+c)` — rational, not Gaussian.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain a term that could produce `epsilon * exp(-(T - c)^2)`, which is a Gaussian function of T multiplied by epsilon. The exponential terms in candidates are either `exp(c*epsilon)` (Gaussian/exponential in epsilon, not T), `exp(T*c)` (exponential in T, not Gaussian), or absent entirely.

Since the GT requires a Gaussian in T (i.e., `exp(-T^2 + ...)`) and no candidate has this functional form, none can match.
